## 1. Rich Froning â€” CrossFit Legend Entering Hyrox

### Background & Legacy

Rich Froning Jr. is the most decorated athlete in CrossFit history: 4x individual CrossFit Games champion (2011â€“2014) and 6x team champion with CrossFit Mayhem Freedom. He operates CrossFit Mayhem in Cookeville, Tennessee, runs the Mayhem Athlete online programming platform, and hosts *The Rich Froning Podcast*. His mantraâ€”"Faith. Family. Fitness. Service."â€”frames everything he does.

### Hyrox Race Results & Times

**Based on all available research data, there is no evidence that Rich Froning has competed in an official Hyrox race as of February 2026.** No Hyrox race results, finish times, or event registrations were found bearing his name. The search results consistently return "Rich Ryan" (an Elite 15 Hyrox athlete and host of the RMR Training Podcast) rather than "Rich Froning."

It is critical for the knowledge base to distinguish between these two athletes:

| Athlete | Sport | Notable Achievement |
|---------|-------|-------------------|
| **Rich Froning** | CrossFit | 4x Individual CrossFit Games Champion |
| **Rich Ryan** | Hyrox | Elite 15 qualifier, Pro PR 54:28, Men's Pro Doubles WR holder (48:31 with Pelayo Menendez) |

### Rich Froning's "Going Hybrid" Philosophy

While Froning has not competed in Hyrox, his podcast episode **"Going Hybrid & Doing Hard Things" (Episode 069, January 14, 2026)** reveals his current training trajectory and mindset toward hybrid/endurance events:

- **Iron Man Training**: Froning confirmed he has registered for an **Iron Man triathlon in Panama City, FL (November 7, 2026)**. He stated: *"The reason I'm doing this is because it is so far out of my comfort zone of what I want to do or what I want to be, and I need to do that every once in a while."*
- **Running Background**: He admitted he has never officially completed a marathon, though he once ran 26 miles in training approximately 15 years ago and abandoned marathon preparation because *"I was getting really slowâ€¦ I don't want to be that type of athlete."*
- **21-Mile Trail Run**: He and a crew member ran approximately 21 miles on trails with zero training, zero sleep, and in 19Â°F weatherâ€”demonstrating his raw endurance capacity.
- **Training Plan for Iron Man**: He outlined his approach:
  - Swim twice per week (~2,000m each session), ramping up with one longer open-water session
  - Mountain bike through spring (Amarillo race prep), transitioning to road cycling by July/August
  - One metcon per week with running intervals (5â€“8K)
  - One long slow Sunday session
  - Brick workouts (bike-to-run transitions)

*(Source: The Rich Froning Podcast, Episode 069, CrossFit Mayhem YouTube, Jan 14, 2026)*

### Training Philosophy: General Physical Preparedness (GPP)

Froning's training philosophy is rooted in **GPPâ€”General Physical Preparedness**â€”which aligns philosophically (though not specifically) with hybrid/Hyrox training:

| Training Principle | Froning's Approach |
|---|---|
| **Daily Structure** | 3-hour AM session + 2-hour PM session (during competition season) |
| **Weekly Template** | Mon: Squat / Tue: Press / Wed: Deadlift / Thu: Press / Fri: Squat; Cleans and snatches heavy 2x/week each |
| **Programming Style** | "By the seat of my pants"â€”adjusts daily based on feel, intuitive autoregulation |
| **Conditioning Formats** | AMRAPs, EMOMs, For Time, Interval Training |
| **Periodization** | Base Phase (GPP) â†’ Power Phase (Olympic lifts, plyometrics) â†’ Competition/Peaking Phase |
| **Separation of Modalities** | Keeps strength and conditioning workouts separate; does not mix within a session |

*(Sources: allthingsgym.com, hoylesfitness.com, WHOOP interview, Rich Froning Training Program analysis)*

### Sample Training Days (Documented)

**Day 1:**
- 20 min AirDyne: 30s on / 30s off
- Row 4,500m
- 15 sets EMOM: 3 muscle-ups w/ 20lb vest
- EMOM bench press + power clean ladder to 205lb (reached round 10)
- 3 rounds: handstand walk, double-unders, strict pull-ups, air squats (1 min rest between)
- Power cleans for 25 min: 3 every 30s at 225lb for 5 min

**Day 2:**
- 7 rounds: 7 deadlifts at 275lb + 14 push-ups
- Partner workout: 100 cal Bike Erg / 1,400m Run / 100 cal Bike Erg / 1,400m Run
- 3 rounds (rest 1:1): 3 rope climbs + 21 bench press / 2 rope climbs + 15 bench press / 1 rope climb + 9 bench press (155lb barbell, 30lb backpack rope climb)

*(Source: YouTube "Rich Froning Full Day of Training," allthingsgym.com)*

### Key Insights for the Knowledge Base

1. **Froning has NOT competed in Hyrox**â€”any references to "Rich" in Hyrox contexts likely refer to Rich Ryan.
2. **His GPP background would theoretically translate well** to Hyrox, but he has expressed more interest in Iron Man triathlon and mountain bike racing as his next competitive endeavors.
3. **His training volume (5+ hours/day)** far exceeds what most Hyrox athletes do, but much of it is CrossFit-specific (Olympic lifting, gymnastics).
4. **His self-awareness about running limitations** is instructive: *"I would prefer to do something like Amarillo that sucks still but it's more power output, 30-40 minutes rest for an hour or two."*

## 2. Station-Specific Training Methods (All Elite Athletes)

### 2.1 Sled Work (Push & Pull)

#### Rich Ryan â€” The Sled Transformation Blueprint

Rich Ryan went from being "scared of the sleds" to posting the **fastest sled push time at the 2025 Hyrox World Championships**. His protocol is the most comprehensively documented:

**Three Pillars of Sled Training:**

| Pillar | Focus | Example Session |
|--------|-------|-----------------|
| **Strength** | Heavy load, short distance | Heavy sled Ã— 3-4 sets of 25m, 4-6 min rest between |
| **Speed** | Lighter load, fast turnover | Lighter sled Ã— 50m unbroken, focus on foot speed |
| **Lactate Tolerance** | Race-weight load, unbroken efforts | Race-weight sled Ã— 37-50m unbroken at all costs, long rest (4-6 min), repeat |

**Key Programming Details:**
- **Frequency**: 2x per week (previously tried 4x/week, caused lower leg/foot pain)
- **Progression**: Undulated (not linear)â€”rotates between heavy/short, light/fast, and long/grindy
- **Compromised Work**: One session includes sleds loaded at the FRONT of a compromised running workout (e.g., sled push â†’ tempo run), not after long fatigue accumulation
- **Concentric Advantage**: Sled work is almost entirely concentric (no eccentric loading), meaning faster recovery than squats/deadliftsâ€”a major advantage for frequent training

*(Source: John Get Strong podcast interview with Rich Ryan, "No One's Figured Hyrox Out Yet")*

#### Hunter McIntyre â€” EMOM Sled Protocol

Hunter's signature sled approach uses **time-based EMOM formats** rather than set/rep schemes:

- **18-minute EMOM**: Alternating sled push and TRX rows, flowing continuously (no prescribed restâ€”just maintain sustained lactate threshold effort)
- **Sled weight in training**: 425lb (vs. 340lb race weight for men's pro), deliberately overloading
- **Technique**: High-arm position, lean into sled like a rugby scrum, drive through legs
- **Key principle**: *"As soon as lactate starts to formâ€¦ push a little further and stay there. Don't push so far that performance starts to drop. Sustained burning."*

*(Source: Dan Churchill YouTube, "HYROX Training with 3X World Champion Hunter McIntyre in NYC")*

#### Jake Dearden â€” Structured Week-by-Week Sled Progression

Jake Dearden's published 3-week plan provides the most structured sled periodization:

| Week | Sled Push | Sled Pull |
|------|-----------|-----------|
| **Week 1** | 3 Ã— 25m @ Hyrox weight, 1 min rest | 3 Ã— 25m @ Hyrox weight, 1 min rest |
| **Week 2** | 3 rounds: 25m push + 500m run + 25m push, 90s rest | 3 rounds: 25m pull + 500m run + 25m pull, 90s rest |
| **Week 3** | Full 50m sled push in 5-min window (race simulation) | Full 50m sled pull in 5-min window (race simulation) |

*(Source: Tom's Guide / inkl.com, Jake Dearden 3-week Hyrox plan)*

#### Jason Khalipa â€” CrossFitter's Sled Assessment

Khalipa noted from his Pro Doubles experience (1:07:13 finish):
- The sled was *"surprisingly heavyâ€¦ especially on the pull"*
- The **sled pull is the biggest skill** CrossFitters need to practiceâ€”it's not a movement pattern familiar from CrossFit
- His partner Gabe Yanez had to compensate on burpees because Khalipa took on more sled work

*(Source: Hybrid Fitness Media podcast, "Can HYROX and CrossFit Co-Exist?")*

#### Dan Churchill â€” Learning From Hunter

Dan Churchill trained under Hunter's guidance and noted:
- Hunter's sled push cadence was significantly faster
- Hunter's row stroke rate was ~52 RPM vs. Dan's low 40s, with more power per stroke
- Key takeaway: *"Get faster, stronger, and a better engine"*

*(Source: Dan Churchill YouTube, training session with Hunter McIntyre)*

### 2.2 SkiErg & Rowing

#### Jake Dearden â€” SkiErg Interval Protocol

**Week 1 SkiErg Session:**
- 12 Ã— 250m with 45 seconds rest
- Goal: *"Consistent across all 12 efforts at a tough but repeatable pace"*
- Scale to 8 rounds if accumulated volume is too high

**Week 2 Integration:**
- 3 rounds: 500m Ski Erg + 20m sled push @ Hyrox weight, 90s rest

**Week 3 Race Simulation:**
- 1,000m Ski Erg in a 5-minute window, rest remainder

*(Source: Tom's Guide, Jake Dearden 3-week plan)*

#### Rich Ryan â€” Threshold-Based Erg Training

Rich Ryan's erg approach is driven by his threshold training philosophy:
- SkiErg and RowErg are integrated into **30-minute EMOM sequences** alternating stations every 5 minutes
- Pacing calibrated via **5K erg test** as a threshold baseline
- Key insight: *"The SkiErg matters more than the RowErg on race day"*â€”because heart rate response differs by body position (seated rowing = lower HR due to horizontal leg positioning)
- Common form mistakes addressed on the RMR podcast (damper settings, stroke rate optimization)

*(Source: RMR Training Podcast, "Erg Training for HYROX" episode)*

#### Hunter McIntyre â€” Row/Ski EMOM

**14-Minute EMOM Protocol:**
- 14-minute block on Ski Erg, higher intensity than the 18-min sled block
- "Shorter efforts, higher intensity"â€”fewer total reps, increased power per rep
- Followed by **5 rounds of 20 cal row + 20 burpees in 2-minute windows**

*(Source: Dan Churchill YouTube)*

#### Jason Khalipa / Dan Churchill

No specific SkiErg or rowing protocols were documented for these athletes beyond general race observations. Khalipa acknowledged the erg machines were less of a concern for CrossFit athletes given their familiarity with the equipment.

### 2.3 Wall Balls

#### Rich Ryan â€” The Definitive Wall Ball Strategy

Rich Ryan produced the most comprehensive wall ball guide in the Hyrox space:

**Set/Rep Strategy:**
- If capable of 50+ unbroken: do the big set first, then manage the remainder
- If not: pick a sustainable number (25, 15, or even 5) and maintain consistent rest intervals throughout all 100 reps
- *"Stay just under your threshold for your high-end ability"*

**Breathing Protocol (Counter-Intuitive):**
- **Exhale on release** (throwing the ball up)
- **Inhale on catch/descent**
- This flips the traditional Valsalva squat breathing patternâ€”allows continuous breathing through the full ROM, improves Oâ‚‚ intake, reduces ventilation rate spikes

**Arm Recovery Technique:**
- After throwing the ball, **drop arms down to sides or swing out** to promote blood flow to shoulders
- Do NOT hold arms overhead waiting for the ball to return
- Catch position: under the chin, not above the head

**Cadence Training:**
- Practice **fast descent** into the squatâ€”drop before the ball arrives
- Build "gears"â€”different speeds you can select during the race

**Mental Visualization:**
- Treats every 10 reps as 100m on a running track
- At 60 reps: *"I just have 40 left, which is like 400m. I will never stop in my last 400."*

**Race Pacing Context:**
- Wall balls are the LAST stationâ€”treat the entire race as setup for a "kick" into wall balls
- *"Give back two minutes on the course of your effort so you can come into wall balls and gain two and a half"*

*(Source: Rich Ryan YouTube, "Proven Wall Ball Strategies for HYROX")*

#### Jake Dearden â€” Volume Progression

| Week | Wall Ball Protocol |
|------|-------------------|
| **Week 1** | 4 sets: 30 wall balls @ Hyrox weight in 3-min windows, max farmers carry in remaining time, 2 min rest |
| **Week 2** | 3 rounds: 50 wall balls + 500m run + 50 wall balls, 90s rest Ã— 3 |
| **Week 3** | 100 wall balls in a 5-minute window (race simulation) |

*(Source: Tom's Guide, Jake Dearden 3-week plan)*

#### Hunter McIntyre â€” Training Overload

Hunter uses **20lb wall balls in training** versus the 14lb competition standard (men's pro uses 9kg/~20lb, open uses 6kg/~14lb), creating an overload effect:
- 15 wall balls per minute in EMOM format combined with toes-to-bar
- Emphasis on not "slogging through slow repetitions" but taking **micro breaks, collecting yourself, then attacking again**

*(Source: YouTube, "HYROX Training: Conditioning")*

#### General Wall Ball Endurance Protocols (From Training Literature)

| Protocol | Structure | Focus |
|----------|-----------|-------|
| **Pyramid** | 10-20-30-20-10 reps, 60s rest between | Variable rep schemes |
| **EMOM** | 15 reps every minute Ã— 10 min | Consistent output under time pressure |
| **Tabata Plus** | 8 Ã— 40s on / 20s off, then 2 min rest, repeat 2-3x | Power endurance |
| **Race Simulation** | 100 for time with planned breaks every 20-25 reps | Race-day pacing |

*(Source: hyroxtrainingplans.com)*

### 2.4 Burpee Broad Jumps

#### General Elite Protocols

No athlete in the research dataset provided a detailed, proprietary burpee broad jump training protocol. However, structured approaches from training literature include:

**Technique Optimization:**
- **Drop down**: Controlled fall (not slow descent)
- **Push-up**: Chest to floor, explosive push-off
- **Jump**: Arms back for momentum, triple extension, forward lean
- **Landing**: Bent knees, controlled absorption, quick reset

**Training Progressions:**

| Phase | Protocol |
|-------|----------|
| **Week 1-2** | 5Ã—5 burpees + 5Ã—5 broad jumps separately; 3Ã—10 combined at comfortable pace |
| **Week 3-4** | 4 rounds: 10 BBJ + 90s rest; 3Ã—2 min continuous BBJ |
| **Race-Specific** | Distance pyramids: 20mâ†’40mâ†’60mâ†’80mâ†’60mâ†’40mâ†’20m, 60-90s rest |
| **Sprint Intervals** | 8 Ã— 20m BBJ at high intensity, 45s rest |

**Pacing Strategy:**
- Start at 70-80% maximum intensity
- Focus on rhythm and consistent jump distance
- Build intensity in final 20-30% of distance

*(Source: hyroxtrainingplans.com)*

#### Jason Khalipa â€” Race Lesson

Gabe Yanez (Khalipa's doubles partner) went too hard on burpees to compensate for sled fatigue, then paid for it on the subsequent run: *"I did so many burpees and so fast that we came out of that run and I thought our race was overâ€¦ Jason was actually pulling away from me in the run."* The takeaway: going 10-15 seconds faster on a station costs 2+ minutes on the subsequent run.

*(Source: Hybrid Fitness Media podcast)*

---

### 2.5 Farmers Carry & Sandbag Lunges

#### Jake Dearden â€” Integrated Carry Training

- **Week 1**: 4 sets of 30 wall balls in 3-min windows, then max distance farmers carry @ Hyrox weight in remaining time (2 min rest)
- **Week 2**: Walking lunges: 3 Ã— 50m @ 1.5Ã— Hyrox weight, 2 min rest (overloaded)
- **Week 3**: Full 200m farmers carry and 100m walking lunge in 5-minute windows

*(Source: Tom's Guide, Jake Dearden 3-week plan)*

#### Rich Ryan â€” Lunge Pain Management

Rich Ryan has acknowledged lunges as his biggest pain point, particularly knee-related discomfort. His approach:
- Extended warm-ups before lunge-heavy sessions
- Knees Over Toes Guy (Ben Patrick) programming for joint resilience
- Work with movement specialist Lawrence Van Lingen in Boulder, CO
- Open-minded exploration of non-traditional rehab/prehab methods

*(Source: John Get Strong podcast interview)*

#### Hunter McIntyre & Others

No detailed farmers carry or sandbag lunge protocols were documented for Hunter McIntyre, Jason Khalipa, or Dan Churchill beyond general race execution observations. Hunter's Men's Health profile confirms the standard distances (200m farmers carry, 100m sandbag lunges) but no specific training protocols were published.

## 3. CrossFit-to-Hyrox Translation Guide

### 3.1 What CrossFit Skills Transfer Directly

Based on insights from Jason Khalipa, Rich Ryan, and Gabe Yanez:

| CrossFit Skill | Hyrox Transfer |
|----------------|----------------|
| **Wall balls** | Direct transferâ€”identical movement (though rep count is higher: 100 in Hyrox) |
| **Sled push** | Partial transferâ€”CrossFit athletes familiar with sled but rarely at Hyrox distances |
| **SkiErg / RowErg** | Direct transferâ€”standard CrossFit equipment |
| **Burpees** | Partial transferâ€”Hyrox adds broad jump component |
| **Mental toughness** | Strong transferâ€”*"Doing hard s*** together"* is CrossFit's DNA |
| **Work capacity** | Strong transferâ€”CrossFitters can sustain high output |
| **Strength base** | Strong transferâ€”generally overqualified for Hyrox loads |

### 3.2 Gaps a Typical CrossFit Athlete Has

| Gap | Why It Matters |
|-----|---------------|
| **Running volume & aerobic base** | Hyrox involves 8km of running; CrossFit rarely programs runs >1 mile. Khalipa: *"It's a lot of running."* |
| **Pacing discipline** | CrossFit rewards going all-out; Hyrox punishes it. *"You're gonna pay two minutes on the run if you bake yourself on the stations."* (Gabe Yanez) |
| **Sled pull technique** | Not a standard CrossFit movement. Khalipa identified this as the biggest skill gap. |
| **Sustained threshold effort** | CrossFit metcons are 8-20 min; Hyrox races are 55-75+ min. Rich Ryan: *"I was a middle-distance athleteâ€¦ races between 4 and 15 minutes. Moving into a 60+ minute race is a different style of training."* |
| **Transition management** | Running â†’ immediate station work under high HR is a specific skill. *"Transitions are where races are won or lost."* |

### 3.3 Training Modification Framework

**Phase 1: Base Building (Weeks 1-8)**
- Add 3-4 runs per week (2 easy, 1 tempo, 1 interval)
- Build running volume to 25-35km/week
- Introduce sled pull technique work 2x/week
- Maintain 1-2 strength sessions (reduce Olympic lifting volume)

**Phase 2: Hyrox-Specific (Weeks 9-16)**
- 2x threshold sessions per week (40-55 min at low Zone 4)
- 2x station-specific training (sled circuits, wall ball volume, erg intervals)
- 1x compromised running workout (run + station combos)
- 1x long easy run (10-15km)
- Reduce CrossFit metcons to 1x/week

**Phase 3: Race Peak (Weeks 17-20)**
- Race simulations (partial or full)
- Taper volume 20% in final 2 weeks
- Focus on pacing, transitions, and nutrition strategy

### 3.4 Common Mistakes CrossFit Athletes Make in First Hyrox

| Mistake | Consequence | Fix |
|---------|-------------|-----|
| **Going out too fast** | Blow up by station 5-6; walk the final runs | Start 10-15s/km slower than threshold pace |
| **Sprinting the sleds** | Legs destroyed for remaining 4-5 runs | Short powerful pushes with quick resets; avoid sprinting |
| **Ignoring running training** | Stations feel manageable but total time balloons | Running is ~45% of total race time; train it proportionally |
| **No transition practice** | 10-20 seconds wasted per transition (80-160s total) | Practice runâ†’station combos weekly: 800m run â†’ sled push â†’ 400m run |
| **Treating it like a metcon** | Unsustainable intensity; catastrophic fade | Hyrox is an endurance event with strength elements, not vice versa |
| **Over-relying on strength** | Wasted energy on stations that don't benefit from maximal effort | Efficiency > intensity on stations; save energy for consistent running |
| **Skipping SkiErg/Row practice** | Poor technique costs 60-90s per station | A skilled rower: ~4:00 for 1,000m; beginner with bad form: ~5:30 |

*(Sources: hyroxdatalab.com, Hybrid Fitness Media podcast, RMR Training Podcast, hyroxtrainingplans.com)*

### 3.5 Key Quotes for the Knowledge Base

> **Jason Khalipa**: *"If you come from a CrossFit background, you're not gonna have a problem with any of this stuffâ€¦ the sled's not that heavy. It's the running. It's a lot of running."*

> **Gabe Yanez**: *"If you're a CrossFitter going into it, the stations are not going to be a problem for youâ€”make sure you're pacing the running."*

> **Rich Ryan**: *"If you take a triathlete straight off a triathlon and a CrossFit athlete straight off a competition and make them do a Hyrox, the CrossFitter's probably going to win the first one. But if you train for Hyrox for a year, the triathlete is going to win the next one."*

> **Rich Froning** (on doing hard things outside his comfort zone): *"Nobody does CrossFit anymore. They just run."* (said jokingly about the trend at Mayhem)

> **Hunter McIntyre** (on lactate threshold training): *"When you get to the point where you feel that lactate is starting to form and your muscles are starting to overload, push a little bit further and stay there. Don't push so far that performance starts to drop. Sustained burning."*

**Source: [Rich Froning CrossFit Workout | WOD](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UTNh6jU1lE0)**
This workout is designed for anyone. It's a CrossFit-inspired metabolic-conditioning circuit. There's a push, a pull, and a cardio element. As soon as your push gets uncomfortable, move to the pull. When the pull becomes an issue, move to the jump rope. Jumping rope will make you tired and challenge your forearms just enough to make the other two movements a bit harder.

â€¦

You'll begin with shoulder to overhead (STO). After you complete 15 reps, you'll go directly to pull-ups (PU) and do 15 reps. After you're done with pull-ups, you'll do 30 double-unders (DU).When you're done with the DUs, return to STO and do 12 reps. Then you'll do 12 reps of PUs and another 30 reps of DUs. You'll keep repeating that pattern. The STO and PUs will go down by three reps each set, while the double-unders remain constant at 30 reps.

**Source: [Hyrox - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyrox)**
In 2024, Hyrox announced a relay event with representatives from 20 different countries as captains, with the freedom to pick their teams from any athlete of that country. At the World Championships in Nice, France, the relay will take place as the final event with the winning team taking home $20,000 in prize money ($5,000 per athlete).

â€¦

Qualification for the four major events is based on automatic qualifiers from previous seasons (U.S. Champion, European Champion, Top 3 at World Championships) and the remaining spots are filled in based on time from Pro Division events.

The average finishing time for the men in the Pro division was 1 hour and 22 minutes in 2025.

**Source: [How to Build Endurance for HYROX Wall Balls and Burpees](https://www.hyroxtrainingplans.com/blog/how-to-build-endurance-for-hyrox-wall-balls-and-burpees)**
## Building Wall Ball Endurance

### Technical Foundation for Endurance

**Efficient Movement Pattern:** **Squat Depth**: Full depth to avoid no-reps while conserving energy **Ball Position**: Catch at chest, don't let ball drop below sternum **Throwing Angle**: Consistent target hitting minimizes wasted energy **Breathing Pattern**: Exhale during throw, inhale during squat

**Energy Conservation Techniques:** **Smooth Rhythm**: Consistent rep timing prevents energy spikes **Minimal Pause**: Brief hesitation at bottom, avoid complete stops **Target Focus**: Accurate throws eliminate adjustment energy **Body Position**: Stay close to wall, optimize throwing angle

â€¦

## Building Burpee Broad Jump Endurance

### Technical Efficiency for Endurance

**Burpee Component Optimization:** **Drop Down**: Controlled fall, not slow descent **Push-Up**: Chest to floor, explosive push off **Jump Up**: Efficient feet-to-hands transition **Preparation**: Set up for explosive broad jump

**Broad Jump Component:** **Takeoff**: Athletic position, arms back for momentum **Flight**: Forward lean, triple extension power **Landing**: Bent knees, controlled absorption **Reset**: Quick preparation for next burpee

â€¦

### Progressive Burpee Endurance Training

**Phase 1: Movement Integration (Weeks 1-2)**

**Component Practice:**

- 5 x 5 burpees focusing on smooth transitions

- 5 x 5 broad jumps for consistent distance

- 3 x 10 burpee broad jumps at comfortable pace

- Emphasis on flow and rhythm development

â€¦

- 4 rounds: 10 burpee broad jumps + 90 seconds rest

- Focus on maintaining power output across rounds

- Monitor jump distance consistency

- Build lactate tolerance with moderate volumes

**Time-Based Training:**

- 3 x 2 minutes continuous burpee broad jumps

- Count distance covered in each segment

- Rest 90 seconds between efforts

- Track efficiency and endurance together

â€¦

### Burpee Broad Jump Training Protocols

**Protocol 1: Distance Pyramids**

- 20m â†’ 40m â†’ 60m â†’ 80m â†’ 60m â†’ 40m â†’ 20m

- Rest 60-90 seconds between distances

- Focus: Progressive distance with maintained intensity

- Track: Time and jump consistency at each distance
**Protocol 2: Sprint Intervals**

- 8 x 20m burpee broad jumps at high intensity

- Rest 45 seconds between intervals

- Focus: Maximum power maintenance across efforts

- Application: Build capacity for race-pace efforts

**Protocol 3: Endurance Blocks**

- 4 x 40m burpee broad jumps

- Rest 2 minutes between blocks

- Focus: Sustained power over moderate distances

- Mental: Practice positive self-talk during difficulty

â€¦

### Pacing Strategies for Burpee Broad Jumps

**Conservative Pacing:**

- Start at 70-80% maximum intensity

- Focus on rhythm and consistent jump distance

- Build intensity in final 20-30% of distance

- Benefits: Energy conservation, technique maintenance

**Source: [Common Beginner Mistakes in HYROX (And How to Avoid ...](https://hyroxdatalab.com/articles/common-beginner-mistakes-hyrox)**
## 6. Not Practicing Transitions

**The Mistake:**

You train runs and stations separately. On race day, you realize running â†’ immediate station work is brutal.

**Why It's Bad:**

**Transitions are where races are won or lost.** Going from high heart rate running to technical station work while gasping for air is a skill. If you haven't practiced it, you'll waste 10-20 seconds per transition standing around catching your breath.
**The Fix:**

**Practice "run + station" combos in training:**

- Run 800m at race pace â†’ SkiErg 500m â†’ Run 400m

- Run 1km â†’ Sled Push 50m â†’ Run 800m

- Run 1km â†’ Row 500m â†’ Run 1km

Get comfortable with the heart rate spike and the mental adjustment. Your body adapts.

## 7. Skipping SkiErg and Row Practice

**The Mistake:**

"I'm a good runner, I'll just push through the cardio machines."

**Why It's Bad:**

**Technique matters.** A skilled rower can finish 1000m in 4:00. A beginner with bad form? 5:30. That's **90 seconds lost** on one station.

â€¦

## The Beginner Success Formula

**Avoid these mistakes:**

âœ… Start slow (10-15s/km slower than you think)

âœ… Warm up properly (90 min early, full routine)

âœ… Master sled and lunge technique

âœ… Practice transitions (run + station combos)

âœ… Work on your weak stations (2Ã— per week)

# Every Details Matters - How Rich Ryan executes his Key Quality HYROX Sessions

This past week, I finally hit a major milestone in my Hyrox-inspired training: an 8.5-kilometer threshold run at a 3:14â€“3:15 /km pace, immediately followed by a punishing 30-minute EOM (Every One Minute) sequence, capped off with
**100 wall balls**. Over the last four to five weeks, I gradually built volume and intensity, culminating in todayâ€™s â€œmonsterâ€ session. **8.5 km Threshold Run**at 3:14â€“3:15 /km **30-Minute EOM Sequence**(alternating stations every five minutes) **100 Wall Balls**to finish

â€¦

1â€“5 km: 3:14â€“3:15 (steady threshold)

5â€“7 km: 3:16â€“3:17 (fatigue accumulates)

7â€“8.5 km: 3:18â€“3:20 (tough final push)

**Source: [How to Build Endurance for HYROX Wall Balls and Burpees](https://www.hyroxtrainingplans.com/blog/how-to-build-endurance-for-hyrox-wall-balls-and-burpees)**
### Station-Specific Physiology

**Wall Balls (100 reps):** **Duration**: 4-8 minutes depending on fitness level **Primary Limiters**: Leg power, shoulder endurance, lactate tolerance **Movement Pattern**: Squat + overhead throw + catch coordination **Metabolic Profile**: 70% glycolytic, 30% aerobic contribution

â€¦

## Building Wall Ball Endurance

### Technical Foundation for Endurance

**Efficient Movement Pattern:** **Squat Depth**: Full depth to avoid no-reps while conserving energy **Ball Position**: Catch at chest, don't let ball drop below sternum **Throwing Angle**: Consistent target hitting minimizes wasted energy **Breathing Pattern**: Exhale during throw, inhale during squat

**Energy Conservation Techniques:** **Smooth Rhythm**: Consistent rep timing prevents energy spikes **Minimal Pause**: Brief hesitation at bottom, avoid complete stops **Target Focus**: Accurate throws eliminate adjustment energy **Body Position**: Stay close to wall, optimize throwing angle

### Progressive Wall Ball Endurance Training

**Phase 1: Movement Quality (Weeks 1-2)**

**Technical Development:**

- 5 x 10 wall balls focusing on perfect form

- Rest 2 minutes between sets

- Film technique and analyze consistency

- Use lighter ball (6-8kg) to establish patterns

â€¦

**Time-Based Training:**

- 3 x 3 minutes continuous wall balls

- Count total reps completed in each segment

- Rest 2 minutes between efforts

- Track rep consistency across time periods

**Phase 3: Race-Specific Endurance (Weeks 5-8)**

**High-Volume Sets:**
- 3 x 50 wall balls building toward race pace

- Rest 3 minutes between sets

- Practice strategic breaking within sets

- Develop mental strategies for high-rep endurance

**Fatigue Integration:**

- Wall balls after other challenging exercises

- Example: 400m run + 30 wall balls Ã— 4 rounds

- Practice technique maintenance under pre-fatigue

- Simulate race-order placement and demands

### Wall Ball Endurance Protocols

**Protocol 1: Pyramid Training**

- Round 1: 10 wall balls

- Round 2: 20 wall balls

- Round 3: 30 wall balls

- Round 4: 20 wall balls

- Round 5: 10 wall balls

- Rest 60 seconds between rounds

- Focus: Variable rep schemes with consistent quality
**Protocol 2: EMOM (Every Minute on the Minute)**

- 15 wall balls every minute for 10 minutes

- Adjust reps based on fitness level (10-20 per minute)

- Focus: Consistent output under time pressure

- Recovery: Use remaining time in each minute for rest

**Protocol 3: Tabata Plus**
- 8 rounds: 40 seconds wall balls, 20 seconds rest

- Count reps each round, aim for consistency

- Rest 2 minutes after 8 rounds

- Repeat entire sequence 2-3 times

- Focus: Power endurance under extreme fatigue

**Protocol 4: Race Simulation**

- 100 wall balls for time with strategic breaking

- Plan break points in advance (every 20-25 reps)

- Practice race-day pacing and mental strategies

- Include in larger race simulation sessions

**Source: [Rich Froning Training Program Pdf](https://former-students.imperial.edu/wwu15/article?trackid=dVU72-2672&title=rich-froning-training-program-pdf.pdf)**
### Chapter 1: Programming Principles: The Backbone of Froning's Success

Rich Froning's training isn't random; it's strategically structured around periodization, cycling intensity and volume to optimize results and prevent overtraining. His programs incorporate distinct phases, often featuring:
Base Phase: This foundational phase focuses on building a strong base of general physical preparedness (GPP). It emphasizes foundational movements like squats, presses, deadlifts, and pull-ups at moderate intensities and volumes. The goal is to establish a solid foundation of strength and endurance before progressing to more specialized training. Think high reps, moderate weight, and a focus on technique refinement.

â€¦

Power Phase: This phase incorporates plyometrics, Olympic lifts (like cleans and snatches), and high-intensity movements designed to increase power output. The focus shifts from simply lifting heavy weights to explosively moving weight. This phase builds the capacity for rapid force production, crucial for CrossFit's dynamic movements.

Competition/Peaking Phase: This phase meticulously tapers the training volume while maintaining intensity. The goal is to peak physically and mentally for competitions or major fitness goals. This phase often incorporates specific workouts simulating the demands of the competition or target event. This phase requires careful monitoring to avoid overtraining or injury.
This cyclical approach prevents plateaus and ensures the body is adequately prepared for the demands of each training phase. The constant variation prevents adaptation and fosters continuous improvement.

â€¦

### Chapter 3: Metabolic Conditioning: Building Unrivaled Endurance

Froning's conditioning isn't just about running; it's about building a highly efficient cardiovascular system and exceptional work capacity. His program uses various high-intensity interval training (HIIT) methods:

AMRAP (As Many Rounds/Reps As Possible): This time-based format pushes athletes to complete as many rounds or repetitions of a given workout as possible within a set timeframe. This maximizes caloric expenditure and cardiovascular stress.
EMOM (Every Minute On the Minute): This involves completing a set number of repetitions of an exercise within each minute, resting the remainder of the minute. This is excellent for building both strength and endurance simultaneously.

For Time: These workouts are designed to be completed as quickly as possible, maximizing both strength and conditioning simultaneously. The focus is on speed and efficiency.

Interval Training: Alternating high-intensity bursts with periods of active or passive recovery. This method improves both aerobic and anaerobic capacity.

The intensity of these workouts is high, but the programming is carefully designed to prevent overtraining and allow for adequate recovery.

## Listen to Your Body

CrossFit famously believe in a randomised approach to exercise and nobody personifies this more than Rich Froning. In one documentary I watched about him, when asked how he does his programming he replied â€œby the seat of my pantsâ€. Itâ€™s the embodiment of listening to your body.

Daily workouts are adjusted depending on how he feels on a given day. This almost casual approach to programming means stress levels are kept lower as he wonâ€™t ever feel as though he didnâ€™t do what he

â€¦

## Clear Workout Focus

Rich Froning trains multiple times per day (3-6 daily workouts), and each one has a clear focus. He doesnâ€™t seem to â€˜mix modalitiesâ€™ within a workout, for example he keeps his strength workouts and his conditioning workouts separate.

Contrast this with a typical gym goer, who may spend 20 minutes on a bike or treadmill and then try to lift weights. Would they be lifting as well as they possibly could having already done 20 minutes work? I doubt it. That means the potential improvements in stamina and strength have both been blunted.
